Canonical req.json() body-parse exception class) → **179** (V2 mandatory pre-mortem dissent gate 2026-05-16 — premortem-defence route req.json() body-parse + the teamMember orgId fail-soft lookup, which mirrors the existing outcome-route pattern verbatim, + PremortemDefenceCaptureCard res.json() error-body parse ×2; all canonical body-parse / orgId-resolve exception classes — no delivery/audit/flywheel path swallowed) → **182** (Outreach Intel Brief · Phase A 2026-05-17 — IntelBriefPanel `res.json().catch(() => null)` body-parse + intel-brief read route `@schema-drift-tolerant` `findFirst().catch(() => null)` (pre-migration envs) + intel-brief.ts per-category `searchNews().catch(() => [])` degraded-mode fallback so one feed-category read failing can't sink the whole brief; all canonical fire-and-forget classes — no delivery/audit/flywheel path swallowed) → **183** (Outreach 1-pager · Phase C 2026-05-17 — IntelBriefPanel `generateOnepager` `res.json().catch(() => null)` error-body parse before throwing; canonical req.json()/res.json() body-parse exception class) → **187** (Defensibility Vector 1 · 2026-05-17 — `OperationalProxyResolutionCard` captureProxy + resolveProxy `res.json().catch(() => null)` body-parse ×2 + `/api/containers/[id]/proxy-resolution` `request.json().catch(() => null)` body-parse + the teamMember orgId fail-soft lookup that mirrors the outcome route verbatim; all canonical body-parse / orgId-resolve exception classes — no delivery/audit/flywheel path swallowed) → **188** (friction audit #2 · OrgRoiCard 2026-05-17 — the `res.json().catch(() => null)` body-parse on the `/api/analytics/roi` fetch; canonical res.json() body-parse exception class, the card degrades to not-rendered). Wired into pre-commit via `npm run lint:silent-catches`. Codifies the saved memory `feedback-fire-and-forget-exceptions-need-comments` as automation. **Adding a new silent catch requires:** (a) replacing an existing one, (b) upgrading to `log.warn(...)`, OR (c) bumping `SILENT_CATCH_BASELINE` in the script with an inline comment naming the exception class. **Forward-looking discipline (re-locked 2026-05-05):** the 121 → 155 jump happened without per-bump CLAUDE.md prose updates — the script const moved but the documentation didn't. From this point: every baseline bump must (i) edit the const, (ii) leave an inline comment naming the exception class on the line above, AND (iii) update the trajectory line in CLAUDE.md within the same commit. Future audits will re-detect drift by comparing the const value to the prose number; if they diverge by >2, the audit reports that as a CLAUDE.md staleness bug.

**Slop-scan as second quality gate (locked 2026-04-27).** Run `npm run slop-scan` alongside `npx tsc --noEmit` after any non-trivial ship — Tier-N planned-work commits, refactor sprints, anything where `git diff --cached --stat` shows > 10 files changed. Bug-fix singletons don't need it. The script is at [scripts/slop-scan.sh](scripts/slop-scan.sh) and runs the modem-dev/slop-scan v0.3.0 default-pack rules. **Target**: `scorePerKloc < 4.0` (mature-OSS median is 1.48; AI-default median is 10.90; we sit at 3.87 as of the 2026-04-27 cleanup). **Trip-wire**: if `scorePerKloc` regresses commit-over-commit by > 0.5, pause and investigate — that's slop accumulating, not legitimate growth. **Interpretation rules**: (a) `defensive.empty-catch` / `error-obscuring` / `error-swallowing` — check against the fire-and-forget exceptions list (see "Fire-and-forget discipline" lock); if exception applies add an inline comment per the saved memory `feedback-fire-and-forget-exceptions-need-comments`; otherwise upgrade to `log.warn(...)` or fail-closed for commerce. (b) `structure.duplicate-function-signatures` — check if duplication is real per the saved memory `feedback-search-canonical-before-extracting`; if yes extract to a shared utility in `src/lib/utils/` (existing utilities: `grade.ts`, `confidence.ts`, `string.ts`, `request.ts`). (c) `tests.duplicate-mock-setup` — only refactor when mock shapes truly match across ≥3 files; helpers live in [src/test-utils/](src/test-utils/). (d) `structure.directory-fanout-hotspot` / `barrel-density` / `async-noise` — false-positives at our scale; ignore.

**SEVERITY_COLORS canonical-import discipline (locked 2026-05-01).** The `Record<string, string>` map at [src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts](src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts) `SEVERITY_COLORS` is the canonical 4-level severity palette (`critical` → `var(--error)`, `high` → `var(--severity-high)`, `medium` → `var(--warning)`, `low` → `var(--success)`). Five files were carrying local hex copies of the same map — drift class. Migrated 2026-05-01: [SimulatorTab](<src/app/(platform)/documents/[id]/tabs/SimulatorTab.tsx>), [BiasDetailModal](<src/app/(platform)/documents/[id]/BiasDetailModal.tsx>), [DecisionBriefTab](src/components/deals/DecisionBriefTab.tsx), [CaseStudyGraphSection](<src/app/(marketing)/case-studies/[slug]/CaseStudyGraphSection.tsx>), [TeamIntelligenceTab](src/components/ui/TeamIntelligenceTab.tsx). **Tint helper pattern**: the prior `${hex}15` (hex + 1-byte alpha) concatenation no longer works after migration since SEVERITY_COLORS resolves to `var()` expressions. The replacement is a small `severityTint(level, alphaPct)` helper using modern `color-mix(in srgb, ${color} 8%, transparent)` — every evergreen browser DI targets supports it. When introducing a new severity-coloured surface, import the canonical map and the tint helper rather than redefining either. **Files NOT migrated** (different shape, not drift; each is a DOCUMENTED EXCEPTION per the 2026-05-13 V-3 follow-through audit — future audits should skip these without re-flagging): (a) [QuickScanModal](src/components/ui/QuickScanModal.tsx) — `{bg, text}` tuple shape (NOT `Record<string, string>` like canonical); (b) [CaseStudyBiasGraphExport](src/components/founder-hub/content-studio/CaseStudyBiasGraphExport.tsx) — jspdf-rendered hex required for PNG export (`var()` doesn't resolve inside jspdf canvas context); (c) [EnterpriseFrictionMatrix](src/components/founder-hub/sales/EnterpriseFrictionMatrix.tsx) — intentional 3-key map with blue for `medium` representing "manageable" rather than "warning" (semantic divergence is the feature, not a bug); (d) [DocumentTextHighlighter](src/components/visualizations/DocumentTextHighlighter.tsx) — 4-key Tailwind-class tuple (`bg / border / text / underline`) for highlight chrome, NOT CSS var strings. **Files migrated 2026-05-13 (V-3 ship)**: [RippleAlertBanner](src/components/dashboard/RippleAlertBanner.tsx) — uses `Record<RippleSeverity, string>` (subset of canonical 4 keys), projected through `{ high: CANONICAL_SEVERITY_COLORS.high, medium: CANONICAL_SEVERITY_COLORS.medium }` so the canonical lockstep holds without losing the type-narrowed RippleSeverity union.

**Drift-class bug rule (locked 2026-04-27 after the `quick-score.ts:scoreToGrade` find; enforced by lint as of 2026-05-09 evening).** When a constant or algorithm has a canonical source (e.g. `GRADE_THRESHOLDS` in `src/lib/scoring/dqi.ts`, model names in CLAUDE.md model policy, framework counts in `getAllRegisteredFrameworks()`), every consumer MUST import from that canonical source. Re-implementing the same logic in another file IS the drift-class bug — even if it's correct today, it'll diverge silently when one copy gets updated and the others don't. The 2026-04-27 slop-scan sweep caught `quick-score.ts:scoreToGrade` using 90/70/50/30 instead of the canonical 85/70/55/40. The 2026-05-09 hygiene Tier 1.3 sweep caught `conviction.ts:getGrade` using `score >= 50` for C grade instead of `>= 55` — same drift class, six months apart, both fixed. **Now enforced by `scripts/lint-canonical-imports.mjs`** (4th pre-commit gate, locked 2026-05-09). The lint blocks new local re-implementations of: `formatBiasName` / `humanizeBias` / `formatBiasType` / `formatBiasLabel` / `humanizeBiasType` / `formatBiasNameCompact` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/labels`); `severityColor` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/severity`); `gradeFromScore` / `scoreToGrade` / `getGrade` / `dqiGrade` / `gradeFor` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/grade`); `formatDate` / `formatDateTime` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/format-date`); `truncate` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/string`); `extractIp` (canonical: `@/lib/utils/request`). Opt-out: inline `// canonical-exception — <reason>` comment on the same line as `function X(` OR the line above (mirrors the `drift-tolerant` + `@schema-drift-tolerant` patterns in the count + silent-catch + Prisma-schema ratchets). The comment IS the audit trail. **Forward-looking**: when adding a small utility (truncate / extractIp / formatX / colorFor), grep `src/` for an existing equivalent before writing a new one (per saved memory `feedback-search-canonical-before-extracting`); the lint will block you if a canonical exists. When extending the banned-name list, add the entry to `BANNED` in the lint script + add the corresponding canonical export to `src/lib/utils/`.

**Cross-model noise jury — locked 2026-05-06 (extends the 3-frame discipline).** The noise jury now fires across TWO model families by default: native Gemini 3 Flash Preview + Grok 4.3 via Vercel AI Gateway. Frame mapping (per `DEFAULT_NOISE_JURY_MODELS` in [src/lib/agents/nodes.ts](src/lib/agents/nodes.ts)): `analyst_skeptical → gemini-3-flash-preview · regulator_hostile → xai/grok-4.3 · contrarian_strategist → gemini-3-flash-preview` (2:1 Gemini:Grok ratio so a Grok outage degrades to all-Gemini gracefully — jury still functional, single-architecture diversity). The `runJudgeCall(modelName, prompts, options)` helper routes by model-name shape: bare names (`gemini-3-flash-preview`) hit the native GoogleGenerativeAI SDK + `gemini` circuit breaker; provider-prefixed names (`xai/grok-4.3`, `google/gemini-3-pro`) route through the AI Gateway via `providers/gateway.ts` + the new `gateway` circuit breaker (separate failure domain so Gemini outages can't poison Grok and vice versa). Variance measured: stochastic (random seed) + architectural (2 model families) + framing (3 professional lenses) = three orthogonal axes. **Cost impact**: Grok 4.3 ≈ $3/1M input, $15/1M output (per xAI public pricing 2026-05); the regulator_hostile frame is the most-load-bearing single frame, so spending ~2× on that arm vs the others is the right cost/quality trade. **Override**: `NOISE_JURY_MODELS` env var (comma-separated 3-model list); empty falls through to the default. **Disclosure**: cost-tracker entries for `xai/grok-4.3` and `google/...`-prefixed gateway models added to [cost-tracker.ts](src/lib/utils/cost-tracker.ts) `TOKEN_COSTS` so per-audit cost estimation stays honest. **Required env vars**: `AI_GATEWAY_API_KEY` (Vercel — set in Production + Preview); without it the gateway calls fail-closed via the gateway circuit breaker and the surviving Gemini frames carry the jury (degraded mode, logged via `Noise judge failed` warn).

**Noise-jury 3-frame discipline (locked 2026-05-01).** The noiseJudgeNode in [src/lib/agents/nodes.ts](src/lib/agents/nodes.ts) used to fire 3 calls with the SAME prompt across (optionally) different model architectures — measuring stochastic + architectural variance only. The 2026-05-01 audit critique was correct: "3 calls to the same model are not independent judges; they're 3 samples from the same distribution." The fix landed in the same audit response: [src/lib/agents/prompts.ts](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts) now exports `NOISE_JUDGE_FRAMES` — a 3-frame array (`analyst_skeptical` / `regulator_hostile` / `contrarian_strategist`) that applies the SAME 0-100 scoring rubric and SAME output JSON shape through three DIFFERENT professional lenses (equity-research, GC + Basel III ICAAP, Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 reference-class skepticism). Combined with the existing 2-model architectural diversity (`gemini-3-flash-preview` + `gemini-3.1-flash-lite` per the 2026-04-24 NOISE_JURY_MODELS lock) and the random-seed appended at call time, the jury now measures THREE orthogonal sources of variance: stochastic, architectural, framing. **Disagreement interpretation**: low stdDev across the 3 frames → robust quality (the document survives multiple lenses); high stdDev → framing-sensitive quality (it survives one lens but collapses under another, which is itself the noise signal — tells the reviewer which audience will be harshest). The investment-noise overlay (`buildInvestmentNoiseOverlay(state.documentType)`) is now layered onto each frame's prompt rather than the legacy single base prompt, so all 3 frames score against the same strategic-decision context. Legacy `NOISE_JUDGE_PROMPT` retained as a single-judge fallback only — never used by the production jury path. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a new frame, hold the output JSON schema identical so the noiseJudgeNode parser + benchmark-extraction path stays unchanged; the frame variation is a system-prompt swap, not a downstream schema change. When adding a new model to NOISE_JURY_MODELS, the frame mapping is positional (frame[i] uses model[i]) — keep the array lengths aligned.

**Count-drift ratchet (locked 2026-05-01; baseline ratcheted 2026-05-02 from 90 → 82 after the framework-count + Sparring-rubric + Education-deck sweep removed 8 stale literals; ratcheted 2026-05-06 from 82 → 81 after the CorePipelineTab cross-model-jury copy update; ratcheted 2026-05-11 from 80 → 77 after the CLAUDE.md archive split moved Phase 1 + Phase 2 + Phase 3.5 + AI Copilot ship-log prose to `docs/CLAUDE-archive-2026-Q2.md` — 3 count literals retired from the scanned working set; ratcheted 2026-05-17 from 77 → 75 after the M-1 residual cascade / U-3.1 migrated the founder-school + competitive-positioning `N regulatory frameworks` literals to `${FRAMEWORK_COUNT}` interpolation — two fewer hardcoded counts).** Linter at [scripts/lint-counts.mjs](scripts/lint-counts.mjs) scans `src/` + `CLAUDE.md` + `TODO.md` for hardcoded literals matching `/(\d{1,3})\s+(biases|frameworks|cases|case studies|pipeline nodes|judges|models)/i` and fails when the count exceeds the baseline. The const at [scripts/lint-counts.mjs](scripts/lint-counts.mjs) line 70 is the source of truth — read it, do not trust this prose. Wired into pre-commit via `npm run lint:counts`. Codifies five prior count-drift audits (2026-04-25 framework + bias counts, 2026-04-27 StartHereTab, 2026-04-28 EnhancedEmptyState, 2026-04-29 framework-count derivation, 2026-05-02 framework + Sparring-rubric + Education-deck sweep) as automation. **Adding a new count literal requires:** (a) interpolating from the canonical (`${BIAS_COUNT} biases`, `${FRAMEWORK_COUNT} frameworks`, `${HISTORICAL_CASE_COUNT} cases`), (b) using `getAllRegisteredFrameworks().length` directly, (c) adding `// drift-tolerant — <one-line reason>` on the same line OR the line above (the marker IS the audit trail), (d) replacing an existing literal. The baseline covers the scoped subset counts (e.g. "10 frameworks across African markets"), historical timeline references, content quotes citing specific case studies, and known-stable canonical references — implicitly drift-tolerant via baseline. **Forward-looking rule**: prefer interpolation; reach for `drift-tolerant` only when the literal is genuinely fixed (a quote, a sprint deliverable count, an architectural constant scoped to a non-canonical subset). **Forward-looking discipline (re-locked 2026-05-07)**: every baseline bump must (i) edit the const at `scripts/lint-counts.mjs` line 70, (ii) leave an inline comment naming the migration class on the line above, AND (iii) update the prose ratchet history above within the same commit. Prose-vs-const drift > 2 = CLAUDE.md staleness bug.

## Project Structure

```
src/
├── app/
│   ├── (marketing)/     # Public pages: landing, case-studies, taxonomy, privacy, terms
│   ├── (platform)/      # Authenticated dashboard (all under /dashboard/*)
│   │   ├── dashboard/   # 25+ page routes
│   │   └── documents/   # Document detail page with analysis tabs
│   ├── api/             # 70+ API routes
│   ├── login/           # Auth
│   └── shared/          # Public share links
├── components/          # 200+ React components
│   ├── ui/              # Core design system (shadcn + custom)
│   ├── founder-hub/     # 16 tab components for Founder Hub
│   ├── analysis/        # Analysis display components
│   ├── settings/        # IntegrationMarketplace, AuditLogInline
│   └── ...              # Domain-grouped components
├── lib/
│   ├── agents/          # LangGraph pipeline (nodes.ts, graph.ts, prompts.ts)
│   ├── ai/              # Model router + Gemini/Claude providers
│   ├── compliance/      # 7 regulatory frameworks
│   ├── scoring/         # DQI computation (dqi.ts — 792 lines)
│   ├── learning/        # Causal learning, outcome scoring, bias genome
│   ├── replay/          # Score decomposition + counterfactual engine
│   ├── integrations/    # Slack, Google Drive, email, webhooks
│   ├── constants/       # Bias taxonomy (bias-education.ts), case studies
│   └── utils/           # Logger, cache, encryption, rate-limit, etc.
├── hooks/               # 20+ custom React hooks
├── types/               # TypeScript interfaces
└── proxy.ts             # CSRF, session management (Next.js 16 — middleware.ts is deprecated)
```

## Critical Conventions — READ THESE

### Styling

- **Use CSS variables with fallbacks**, not hardcoded hex colors or dark-mode Tailwind classes:

  ```tsx
  // ✅ Correct
  style={{ color: 'var(--text-primary)', background: 'var(--bg-card)' }}

  // ❌ Wrong — breaks in light theme
  className="text-white bg-white/5 border-white/10"
  ```

- Full token system defined in `src/app/globals.css` (297 lines). Key tokens:
  - Backgrounds: `--bg-primary`, `--bg-secondary`, `--bg-tertiary`, `--bg-card`, `--bg-elevated`
  - Text: `--text-primary`, `--text-secondary`, `--text-muted`, `--text-highlight`
  - Accent: `--accent-primary` (#16A34A green), `--accent-secondary`, `--accent-tertiary`
  - Severity: `--success`, `--warning`, `--error`, `--info`, `--severity-high`, `--severity-critical`
  - Borders: `--border-color`, `--border-active`, `--border-hover`, `--border-primary` (alias for `--border-color`; used by ~114 refs across Founder Hub + analytics components — must stay defined in BOTH `:root` and `.dark` blocks, otherwise those components fall through to browser default #333 in light theme)
  - Shadows: `--shadow-sm`, `--shadow-md`, `--shadow-lg`, `--liquid-shadow`
  - Radius: `--radius-sm` (4px), `--radius-md` (8px), `--radius-lg` (12px), `--radius-xl` (16px), `--radius-full` (9999px)
- **Dark mode posture (locked 2026-04-23):** The product runs exclusively in light theme. The `.dark` class + next-themes toggle still exist in the codebase, and `.dark` selectors still resolve, but no active work goes into dark-mode QA. Rules: (1) do not add new dark-only hex colors or `.dark`-scoped overrides on platform pages, (2) do not propose a full dark-mode QA sprint unless an enterprise buyer explicitly demands it, (3) do not strip the `.dark` CSS in a surprise PR — the cost of the current posture is near-zero maintenance, the cost of stripping is days of migration + regression surface. Revisit the kill-or-ship question only when an investor or design partner asks for dark mode, or when the pre-seed round closes. Interior dark classes inside severity wrappers in `src/components/visualizations/*` (CausalDAG, GraphDetailPanel, RiskHeatMap, ToxicCombinationCard, DecisionTimeline, ClusterSummaryPanel, StakeholderMap) are intentional per the light-theme audit rule and are NOT bugs.
- **Marketing mega-menu nav (locked 2026-04-23):** Single shared component [MarketingNav](src/components/marketing/MarketingNav.tsx) renders the public top bar on every marketing surface (landing + 11 other pages). Three mega-menu sections (Platform / Proof & Research / Enterprise) plus flat Pricing plus right-side CTAs (Sign In / Book a call / Try the Demo). Each mega panel has a link column on the left and a featured dark card on the right. **Open/close behavior**: hover-to-open + click-to-toggle on desktop with a 150ms grace period between trigger and panel so users can traverse into the panel without it snapping shut; click-outside or Escape closes. **Mobile**: hamburger → accordion, each section expands in place. `MarketingNav` also exports `BRAND_COLORS` (the `C` palette object) for the three marketing pages that import it alongside. Legacy `CaseStudyNav` component was deleted in the same commit — do not reintroduce a separate marketing nav; every new marketing page uses `<MarketingNav />`.
- **Marketing display font (locked 2026-04-23):** `Instrument_Serif` (Regular + Italic) registered as `--font-display` in [layout.tsx](src/app/layout.tsx). Applied via the `.marketing-display` utility on the landing hero H1. Rule: use on marketing H1/occasional H2 only, never on platform / dashboard surfaces (Inter stays the workhorse for body + every authenticated page). The switch is the single highest-leverage visual move against the "default-Inter SaaS template" perception — one font pair, one utility class, massive perception shift. When writing new marketing H1s, reach for `.marketing-display` by default.
- **Em-dash discipline (enforced 2026-04-23, re-swept 2026-05-01):** `&mdash;` and `—` in marketing copy are capped at one per page, reserved for emphasis. Do NOT write two em dashes in the same paragraph; use commas, periods, or parentheticals. Standard replacements: `A — B — C` → `A, B, C` or `A. B. C.` (em-dash-around-parenthetical pattern is the worst offender; replace with actual parentheses). JSX comments are exempt (developer-facing). JS/TS multi-line comments (`/* ... */`) and JSDoc are also exempt — only USER-VISIBLE prose counts. Label separators like "EU AI Act · high-risk decision-support obligations" use the middle dot `·`, not an em dash. **2026-05-01 sweep**: /security had 3 user-visible em-dashes (in VENDOR_CONTINUITY incorporation-roadmap body, TRIAL_DATA_HANDLING no-training body, trial-data SectionHeader body); all 3 swept to commas / colons. /privacy has 1 (anonymizer first-node line — at the cap). When adding new marketing copy, keep user-visible vs comment-block distinction visible in your head; the count includes only user-visible. **2026-05-15 sweep**: the 2026-05-01 "landing has 1 user-visible (McKinsey 8% &mdash;)" note went stale when the hero was re-locked 2026-05-07 to the 3-card flow (that mdash is gone). Current landing user-visible em-dash count audited = the PATTERN mini-card's 3-item `term — definition` list (Synergy Mirage / Conglomerate Fallacy / Winner's Curse). All 3 swept to colons (the correct enterprise-voice punctuation for term:definition; an em-dash there is the lock's "worst offender" separator pattern). **Landing is now 0 user-visible em-dashes** — every remaining `—`/`&mdash;` token in `(marketing)/page.tsx` is inside a `{/* */}` JSX comment or a `//` / `/* */` JS comment (exempt). Future audits: re-grep user-visible only; do not re-flag the comment tokens.
- **Landing hero shape (re-locked 2026-05-07 evening — sign-in-first 3-card flow):** Single-column centered structure at max-width 880px. Stack order: pain-stat tag (italic 13px slate-500, McKinsey 8%/92% framing) → `FOR DECISIONS WORTH DEFENDING` eyebrow → H1 in `.marketing-display` Instrument Serif (italic green fragment "the reasoning audit platform.") → contrast sub-head: **"Most tools audit your data. We audit your reasoning, catching the fatal blind spots in strategic memos before the outcome forces the lesson."** (em-dash removed; second clause reframed around outcomes rather than committee-specifically so audience-fit covers VC IC decisions, Corp Dev deals, board memos, and fund-LP reviews uniformly) → primary CTA **`Start your first audit`** routing to `/login?mode=signup&redirect=/dashboard?onboarding=1` (sign-in-first per the Corgi pattern) + secondary `How it works` text-link + tertiary `See an audit we already ran →` text-link routing to `/demo` (cold-evidence door for readers who don't yet trust DI to deserve their email) → **3-card `hero-mini-cards` horizontal row centered max-880px**: (a) PROBLEM red top-border + AlertCircle, big mono `70-90%` + "of M&A and venture deals miss their thesis. Most failures trace back to bias patterns visible in the original memo nobody named at the time" + tiny italic source line `HBR · KPMG`; (b) PATTERN amber top-border + Search icon, big "Same four biases" + "Confirmation, anchoring, sunk cost, narrative coherence — the most common patterns behind deal failures. Hard to spot from inside the document; easy to surface from outside" (the from-inside / from-outside framing makes the audit's value STRUCTURAL not corrective; never team-blaming); (c) SOLUTION green top-border + ShieldCheck, big mono `60` + "second pre-emptive audit. Biases named, counterfactuals quantified, the record signed and shareable before the deal moves forward" → full-width static `HeroCredibilityStrip` (5 signals: R²F · AI Verify · SOC 2 Type II infrastructure · 19 regulatory frameworks · Brier 0.258 calibration). Mobile <900px stacks the 3 mini-cards to single column. **Three-door pattern**: warm intent (Door 1) → hero CTA → sign-in → onboarding-as-demo; cold curiosity (Door 2) → tertiary link → /demo specimen; procurement (Door 3) → Book a call. **The rules**: clarity over cleverness; outcome-fit over committee-fit; structural framing over team-blaming framing; pain → mechanism → solution as a 3-card flow. Founder feedback that anchored this: "even on YC-funded startup pages, clarity is always what triumphs over everything else." The legacy `HeroCounterfactualTease`, the synthetic `SampleAuditCard`, the asymmetric-tail body paragraph, and the right-column `WeWorkProofPanel` are all retired; do not reintroduce. WeWorkProofPanel component lives at [src/components/marketing/proof/WeWorkProofPanel.tsx](src/components/marketing/proof/WeWorkProofPanel.tsx), mounted on /demo only.

- **Sign-in-first auth flow + magic-link primary (locked 2026-05-07 evening — the Corgi pattern adapted for DI):** the entire anonymous-demo-then-signup funnel was inverted to sign-in-first, with magic-link as the primary email-auth method. **Hero CTA**: `Start your first audit` → `/login?mode=signup&redirect=/dashboard?onboarding=1`. **/demo stays accessible as the cold-evidence door** (Door 2) but is no longer promoted as the primary "try it" path; the WeWorkProofPanel specimen card lives there, plus the existing anonymous paste flow (kept for backwards-compat — not actively promoted). **/login refactored**: new state `authMethod: 'magic' | 'password'` defaults to `'magic'`. Single email field + `Send magic link` button is now the primary form. Password form (the existing email + password handler) is gated behind a `Use password instead` text-link toggle below the form. Magic-link-sent confirmation card with `Use a different email` reset. New handler `handleMagicLinkSend` at [src/app/login/page.tsx](src/app/login/page.tsx) calls `supabase.auth.signInWithOtp({ email, options: { shouldCreateUser: true, emailRedirectTo } })` which unifies sign-in + sign-up via a single email field. Google OAuth stays as the top-of-form primary affordance (unchanged). Terms of Service §3 Account Registration was updated in the same ship to reflect "Google OAuth, email magic link, and email + password. Enterprise customers may use SAML SSO." — the prior copy claimed Google-only. **The strategic logic**: anonymous demos generate impressions, not relationships. Every visitor who pastes at /demo, sees the wow moment, and closes the tab is a customer DI never gets to talk to again. Sign-in-first means email captured upfront, account created, first audit happens INSIDE the product. Higher commitment threshold at the door, dramatically higher retention behind it. Magic-link primary collapses sign-up to a single email field — lowest commitment compatible with sign-in-first. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new entry points to the funnel, default to sign-in-first unless the entry point is explicitly a cold-evidence door (specimen viewer / public DPR PDF / case study). Anonymous-audit flows should be the exception, not the default.

- **Decision Alpha page deleted (2026-05-07 evening):** `/decision-alpha` removed entirely + 308 redirect to `/proof` added in [next.config.ts](next.config.ts). Reasons: (1) the "Published Q2 2026" claim was a recurring-publication promise without any backing workflow at solo-founder scale; (2) the synthetic SECTOR_INDEX values weren't computed from anything; (3) the page carried "30+ biases" count drift vs the canonical 22-bias taxonomy. Removed from landing footer (Product column) + MarketingNav (Proof & Research mega-menu); related TrendingUp lucide icon import cleaned up. Internal `DecisionAlphaTab` in the founder hub stays untouched — different purpose, internal-only. **Forward-looking rule**: do not promote recurring-publication claims (quarterly index / monthly report / weekly digest) as marketing surfaces unless the workflow that produces them actually exists and runs on cadence. A stale "Published Q2 2026" sits worse than no page at all once Q3 / Q4 pass without an update.
- **Type scale (locked 2026-04-23):** Single 1.25 modular scale shared across platform + marketing. Tokens in `globals.css :root`: `--fs-3xs` (11px), `--fs-2xs` (12px), `--fs-xs` (13px), `--fs-sm` (14px), `--fs-base` (16px), `--fs-md` (18px), `--fs-lg` (20px), `--fs-xl` (24px), `--fs-2xl` (24-34px, legacy page-header size), `--fs-page-h1-platform` (28-40px, new `.page-header h1` target), `--fs-page-h1-marketing-hero` (30-48px, landing-hero H1). The platform page-header now uses `--fs-page-h1-platform` so the transition from `/how-it-works` (hero 30-48px) into `/dashboard` (page-header 28-40px) feels continuous rather than a compression step. When adding new platform headings, prefer these tokens over hardcoded `text-3xl`/`text-4xl`/raw `clamp()`.
- Inline `style={{}}` objects are the dominant pattern (not Tailwind utilities). Follow the existing pattern.

### Database

- **Document model uses `uploadedAt`**, NOT `createdAt`, for the creation timestamp. This has caused build errors multiple times — always double-check.
- **Analysis model uses `createdAt`** (standard Prisma).
- Always handle schema drift: wrap Prisma queries in try-catch, check for P2021/P2022 error codes.
- **`@schema-drift-tolerant` comment marker (locked 2026-04-28).** When a `.catch(() => null)` or fallback branch is intentionally tolerating schema drift (table not yet migrated, column added in a later migration than the code path), prefix the inline comment with `@schema-drift-tolerant`. Example: `// @schema-drift-tolerant — pre-3.1 envs return null here`. The marker (a) lets future audits grep `rg "@schema-drift-tolerant"` to skip these intentionally-silent catches, (b) creates a dialect a session can recognise without re-deriving the rationale from prose, (c) integrates with the silent-catch ratchet linter (`scripts/lint-silent-catches.mjs`) — the marker is the audit trail per the `feedback-fire-and-forget-exceptions-need-comments` memory. Adopt the marker on any new schema-drift catch; back-fill on touch when editing a file with an existing schema-drift comment.
- Use `onDelete: Cascade` or `onDelete: SetNull` on all new relations — never leave onDelete unspecified.
- The `recalibratedDqi` field on Analysis is a nullable JSON field (added April 2026).
- **Prisma JSON fields need explicit casting.** When writing objects to nullable JSON columns (e.g., `biasBriefing`, `recalibratedDqi`), inferred types cause `InputJsonValue` errors. Fix: import `{ Prisma } from '@prisma/client'` and cast with `as Prisma.InputJsonValue` (use `Prisma.JsonNull` for explicit null writes). Do NOT use `as unknown as Record<string, unknown>` — `InputJsonValue` is recursive and requires JSON-serializable values, which `Record<string, unknown>` doesn't guarantee.

### Security

- **Always use `safeCompare` from `@/lib/utils/safe-compare`** for secret comparisons. Never write a local implementation — a buggy duplicate was the cause of a critical auth bypass that was fixed.
- CSRF protection is in `src/proxy.ts` — Next.js 16 renamed `middleware.ts` → `proxy.ts` and the export name is `proxy` (not `middleware`). The file at `middleware.ts` still works but emits a deprecation warning on every build. Slack/Stripe/cron paths are exempt.
- Document encryption uses AES-256-GCM via `DOCUMENT_ENCRYPTION_KEY`.
- Slack tokens encrypted with `SLACK_TOKEN_ENCRYPTION_KEY`.
- **Encryption key rotation** uses a `keyVersion` stamp on every encrypted row (`Document.contentKeyVersion`, `SlackInstallation.botTokenKeyVersion`). New keys are provisioned at `DOCUMENT_ENCRYPTION_KEY_V{N}` / `SLACK_TOKEN_ENCRYPTION_KEY_V{N}`; the active version comes from `*_VERSION` env vars (defaults to highest resolvable). Rotate with `npm run rotate:encryption-key -- --domain document --from 1 --to 2` — batched, idempotent, resumable. Legacy `DOCUMENT_ENCRYPTION_KEY` (un-suffixed) is treated as v1 for back-compat. Full protocol in `src/lib/utils/encryption.ts` header.

### Components & Patterns

- Lazy-load heavy components with `dynamic()` from `next/dynamic` (see Founder Hub page for pattern).
- Use `ErrorBoundary` wrapper on all page-level components.
- Use `EnhancedEmptyState` (not legacy `EmptyState`) for empty states. Always pass `showBrief` and `briefContext` for intelligence brief integration.
- Use `AnimatedNumber` from `@/components/ui/AnimatedNumber` for animating numeric values.
- Use `createLogger('ContextName')` for structured logging in API routes and lib code.
- **Fire-and-forget error handling:** Never swallow errors with `.catch(() => {})` on fire-and-forget operations that affect delivery, audit trails, or the learning flywheel (Slack/email nudges, audit-log writes, playbook usage counters, Nudge.deliveredAt stamps, `humanDecision` status transitions, graph edge-weight adjustments). Use `.catch(err => log.warn('specific context:', err))` at minimum. Silent catches ARE still acceptable for: in-memory cache cleanup, schema-drift tolerance (when commented as such), and `req.json().catch(() => null)` body parsing.
- Standardized API responses: use `apiSuccess()` and `apiError()` from `@/lib/utils/api-response.ts`.
- **Unused imports cause build failures.** Next.js strict mode treats them as errors. Always clean up imports after refactoring (e.g., removing `Suspense, lazy` when switching to `dynamic()`).
- **Founder Hub API calls require `founderPass` prop.** Any component calling `/api/founder-hub/*` must receive and pass the `founderPass` string via props from the hub page.
- **Case study slugs:** Use `getSlugForCase()` from `src/lib/data/case-studies/slugs.ts` for URL-safe slugs. Case study URLs: `/case-studies/{slug}`.
- **Landing page hero graph:** `src/components/marketing/HeroDecisionGraph.tsx` — interactive D3-like knowledge graph. The `CaseStudyBiasGraph` at `src/components/marketing/CaseStudyBiasGraph.tsx` is the simpler radial bias web used on case study cards and detail pages.
- **Section heading utility:** use `.section-heading` (globals.css) for inline subheadings inside `.card-body` — uppercase, tracking-widest, muted. Card titles stay as `.card-header h3`.
- **Board-ready PDF export (extended 2026-04-25 with branding):** `src/lib/reports/board-report-generator.ts` (`BoardReportGenerator`). 2-page client-side jsPDF export (exec summary ≤500 chars, DQI card, top-3 biases, simulated CEO question, top mitigation). Wired into `ShareModal` via the optional `onExportBoardReport` prop and triggerable from the Command Palette on any `/documents/:id` page via the `command-palette-export-board-report` window event. The generator now accepts an optional `branding: BoardReportBranding` parameter — `{ orgName?, gcName?, gcTitle?, gcRegistration?, retentionPolicy?, logoBase64? }` — that adds the customer org name to the cover header, optionally renders a base64 logo top-right on page one, appends a GC signature block to the final page when `gcName` or `gcTitle` is supplied, and surfaces a retention-policy footer line. Backwards-compat: omitting `branding` produces the existing default Decision Intel attribution. The Settings → Brand UI to populate this (and a per-org persist for the values) is a follow-up; the generator is ready when the wiring lands.
- **Upload bias preview:** `getBiasPreview(filename, selectedDocType)` from `@/lib/utils/bias-preview` — pure client-side regex → likely biases. Prefer `selectedDocType` over filename when present.
- **R²F paper-application sprint COMPLETE — 10 of 10 detectors shipped (wedge-batch-4 lock 2026-05-07).** Closes the Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint that began 2026-04-30. Final three detectors landed together: **#1 Fractionation of Expertise** (Kahneman & Klein 2009 sub-domain finding) at [src/lib/learning/fractionation-of-expertise.ts](src/lib/learning/fractionation-of-expertise.ts) — pure-function Prisma lookup that slices the user's outcome history by decision class (M&A integration / capital deployment / market entry / long-horizon strategy / operations / unknown) and contrasts this-class to other-class calibration. Closes the Margaret-class "your feedback is sparse FOR WHICH class?" gap that paper-application #6 (Feedback Adequacy) leaves ambiguous. Verdict bands: class_calibrated / broadly_calibrated / fractionated_uncalibrated / broadly_cold_start / cannot_assess. **#4 Improper Linear Models / Decision Rubric** (Dawes 1979 "The Robust Beauty of Improper Linear Models in Decision Making") at [src/lib/learning/decision-rubric.ts](src/lib/learning/decision-rubric.ts) — pure-function regex scan of bias-detective excerpts + summary for structural rubric markers (numbered criteria / weighted criteria / decision matrix / scored alternatives / multi-option comparison / criteria-evaluation phrase / tradeoff structure) AND severity-weighted hits on narrative-coherence biases (illusion_of_validity / inside_view_dominance / narrative_fallacy / confirmation / halo). Verdict bands: explicit_rubric / partial_criteria / narrative_dominant / narrative_only / cannot_assess. **#7 Algorithm Aversion** (Dietvorst, Simmons & Massey 2015 "Algorithm Aversion: People Erroneously Avoid Algorithms After Seeing Them Err" · J. Exp. Psychol. General, doi:10.1037/xge0000033) at [src/lib/learning/algorithm-aversion.ts](src/lib/learning/algorithm-aversion.ts) — pure-function regex scan for ten dismissive-of-quantitative language patterns plus compound-bias-hit elevation (authority_bias / illusion_of_validity / inside_view_dominance / overconfidence at high+ severity). Counter-programs the most common buyer objection ("we don't want AI overruling our CSO") by naming the pattern as a documented decision-making error with citation. Verdict bands: no_aversion_signal / mild_aversion / material_aversion / severe_aversion / cannot_assess. **All three wired through five surfaces in lockstep:** (a) [/api/analysis/[id]/insights](src/app/api/analysis/[id]/insights/route.ts) `AnalysisInsightsResponse` extends with three new fields; (b) [PaperApplicationsCard](src/components/analysis/PaperApplicationsCard.tsx) renders 3 new SignalBlocks (Class-Specific Calibration · Rubric Structure · Algorithm Trust) bringing total to **7 SignalBlocks**; (c) [DprPageThreeR2fStrips](src/components/dpr/pages/DprPageThreeR2fStrips.tsx) gains §4.7 / §4.8 / §4.9 strips bringing DPR cover to **9 R²F strips**; (d) [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) populates all three synchronously from existing biases + summary + Prisma user history — no extra round-trips, no schema migrations; (e) **NEW R²F Detector Atlas** at [src/components/marketing/r2f-standard/R2FDetectorAtlas.tsx](src/components/marketing/r2f-standard/R2FDetectorAtlas.tsx) mounted on [/r2f-standard](<src/app/(marketing)/r2f-standard/R2FStandardClient.tsx>) — a 10-detector dynamic visualization showing every paper application as a clickable card (5×2 grid responsive). Click any → detail panel opens inline with full mechanism description, academic citation + DOI, implementation file path, live product surfaces, AND a **per-detector mini-viz** (10 unique SVG illustrations of the signal shape: validity bands ring, reference-class target, feedback timeline, calibration gap meter, fractionation per-class chart, rubric checklist, algorithm-aversion fork, illusion scatter, prospective-hindsight calendar, inside-vs-outside view bubbles). Side palette colours each card by Kahneman synthesis side: rigor (blue) / recognition (green) / integration (amber). **Five academic anchors with DOIs across the 10 detectors**: Kahneman & Klein 2009 (paper-apps #2 / #3 / #6 / #10) · Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 HBR (#8 / #9) · Klein & Mitchell 1995 (#5) · Dawes 1979 (#4) · Dietvorst, Simmons & Massey 2015 (#7). **Forward-looking rule**: any new R²F detector lands in lockstep with (i) `src/lib/learning/<detector>.ts` pure function, (ii) AnalysisInsightsResponse extension, (iii) PaperApplicationsCard SignalBlock, (iv) DPR strip, (v) provenance-record-data assembler population, AND (vi) atlas data entry in `R2FDetectorAtlas.tsx` `DETECTORS` array including a per-detector mini-viz. The pattern is six surfaces; never ship a detector that lives on only some.

- **R²F paper-application #10 · Calibrated Rejection of Subjective Confidence (locked 2026-05-07, Item 3 of wedge-batch-3):** closes the Kahneman & Klein 2009 sprint to 7 of 10 paper applications shipped (the prior 6 — items #5 / #3 / #6 / #8 / #2 / #9 — locked 2026-04-30). New module at [src/lib/learning/calibrated-rejection.ts](src/lib/learning/calibrated-rejection.ts) — pure-function combination of validity class × feedback adequacy × bias-detective hits on confidence-language patterns (illusion*of_validity / overconfidence_bias / authority_bias / anchoring_bias). Computes (a) `rhetoricalConfidenceScore` (severity-weighted hits, capped at 1.0), (b) `earnedConfidenceScore` (validity-score × feedback-score, ∈ [0, 1]), (c) `calibrationGap = max(0, rhetorical - earned)`, (d) verdict band — `well_calibrated` (gap ≤ 0.20), `mildly_overconfident` (≤ 0.40), `materially_overconfident` (≤ 0.60), `severely_overconfident` (> 0.60), or `cannot_assess` (feedback verdict 'unknown'). The `materially_overconfident` band fires the audit-committee-readiness flag — Margaret-class CSO's most-asked question rendered as a verdict: *"does this memo's confidence match the evidence?"\_ **Wired through three surfaces**: (a) [/api/analysis/[id]/insights](src/app/api/analysis/[id]/insights/route.ts) `AnalysisInsightsResponse` extends with `calibratedRejection`; (b) [PaperApplicationsCard](src/components/analysis/PaperApplicationsCard.tsx) renders a 4th SignalBlock with eyebrow "Confidence Calibration" + verdict label + gap/rhetoric/earned metrics + trigger chips below; (c) DPR cover §4.4 strip [CalibratedRejectionStrip](src/components/dpr/pages/DprPageThreeR2fStrips.tsx) — the section renumbered to 6 strips (Validity / Reference Class / Feedback Adequacy / **Confidence Calibration** / Org Calibration / Counterfactual Impact). [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) populates `calibratedRejection` synchronously from the existing validity + feedback + bias-detective data — no extra DB roundtrip. **Pure function** — same input → same output; no LLM call. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new R²F detectors that build on validity + feedback (e.g. paper applications #1 Fractionation of Expertise, #4 Improper Linear Models, #7 Algorithm-Aversion Counter-programming), follow this same pattern — extend AnalysisInsightsResponse + PaperApplicationsCard SignalBlock + DPR §4.X strip in lockstep so the surfaces never drift. Remaining queued: 3 paper applications (#1, #4, #7).

The existing `#calibration` section gained: investor-grade subtitle on the eyebrow ("investor-diligence answer"), methodology version progression card (legacy 2.0.0 deprecated → 2.0.0-seed current platform baseline → 2.1.0 live audits with validity-aware weight shift → per-org Brier supersedes once outcomes accumulate), reproducibility code block showing the `computePlatformCalibrationBaseline` recipe + the public API endpoint + the deterministic mulberry32 bootstrap seed, and an "Investor diligence answer →" jumplink in the page hero so the section is reachable in one click. New [/calibration](<src/app/(marketing)/calibration/page.tsx>) route is a 308 redirect to `/r2f-standard#calibration` — investor diligence emails / DMs that carry the short URL land on the right anchor. New [MarketingNav](src/components/marketing/MarketingNav.tsx) entry under "Proof & Research" labeled "Calibration baseline" links to `/calibration` (which redirects). **Forward-looking rule**: when the case library or `computeBrierFairPredictedDqi` formula changes, regenerate the snapshot literals in [platform-baseline-snapshot.ts](src/lib/learning/platform-baseline-snapshot.ts); the section's methodology version progression card auto-picks up the new baseline. When a customer org's per-org Brier is ready to supersede the seed, add the org-specific "v2.X.0" entry to the progression card alongside.
- **Inline live co-edit (2026-04-23, hardened 2026-04-25):** On [InlineAnalysisResultCard](src/components/analysis/InlineAnalysisResultCard.tsx), a collapsible "Rewrite a flagged passage" panel sits between the biases list and the Featured Counterfactual. Expands to a textarea + Re-audit button; POSTs to [/api/passages/re-audit](src/app/api/passages/re-audit/route.ts) which runs a single focused Gemini call on the passage and returns `{ biases[], estimatedDqi, delta, disclaimer }`. Deliberately NOT the canonical audit pipeline — passage-level estimate only, ~£0.02-0.05 per call vs ~£0.40 for a full audit. Rate-limited 20/hr/user. **Critical (2026-04-25 audit fix):** the UI surfaces the BIAS-COUNT delta (e.g. "Biases in the revised passage · 1, -3 vs the original (4)"), NOT the numeric `estimatedDqi`. A passage-level DQI proxy can drift from the full-pipeline score; rendering it as a score risks the trust-collapse moment Elena flagged ("co-edit to a B+, re-upload full memo, get a C"). The API still computes `estimatedDqi` for back-compat callers but the consumer in InlineCoEditPanel deliberately doesn't render it — keep that discipline. The component now takes `originalBiasCount` (not `originalScore`) for the comparison.
- **Public Enterprise quote builder (2026-04-25, hardened 2026-04-26):** [/pricing/quote](<src/app/(marketing)/pricing/quote/page.tsx>) is a public mirror of the admin-only enterprise quote builder. Mounts the same [EnterpriseQuoteBuilderClient](src/components/billing/EnterpriseQuoteBuilderClient.tsx) (parameterised with `apiEndpoint`, `backHref`, `backLabel` props) and POSTs to [/api/billing/enterprise-quote-public](src/app/api/billing/enterprise-quote-public/route.ts) — IP rate-limited 5/IP/24h, no auth, requires customerName + plausible contactEmail before generating. **2026-04-26 P0 hardening (persona audit, James + Margaret findings):** the generated PDF now carries (a) a prominent amber-banded NON-BINDING-OFFER disclaimer on page 1 below the title, (b) a full Enterprise Terms Appendix on page 2 — indemnification, SLA per tier (`SLA_TIER_UPTIME` constant), data portability on termination, exit assistance, security-incident SLA, sub-processor change notification, audit rights, governing law with EEA/UK carve-out — and (c) "Page 1 of 2 / Page 2 of 2" labels in the provenance footer. The same provisions are mirrored in [terms/page.tsx](<src/app/(marketing)/terms/page.tsx>) sections 10A–10G + 12 so a reader who reaches the live ToS sees the same terms verbatim. Backwards-compat: the admin route at [/dashboard/settings/billing/enterprise-quote](<src/app/(platform)/dashboard/settings/billing/enterprise-quote/page.tsx>) and admin-only POST [/api/billing/enterprise-quote](src/app/api/billing/enterprise-quote/route.ts) stay untouched. The Pricing page Enterprise card surfaces the public route via a secondary link under the "Contact sales" CTA. `noindex` on the public page so it doesn't compete for search relevance with the rest of the marketing surface. Do NOT remove the disclaimer or appendix — both are load-bearing under common-law offer-acceptance principles.
- **Cross-reference truncation reporting (2026-04-25):** [runCrossReferenceAgent](src/lib/agents/cross-reference.ts) now returns a `truncationReport` field on `CrossRefRunOutput` listing per-doc truncation + total-cap exclusions. Caps lifted from 60K/12K chars to 150K/25K chars per doc (gemini-3-flash-preview window has plenty of headroom; chunked multi-pass remains a future option for larger deal rooms). Both [decisions/CrossReferenceCard](src/components/decisions/CrossReferenceCard.tsx) and [deals/CrossReferenceCard](src/components/deals/CrossReferenceCard.tsx) render a "Partial scan" banner when truncation occurred — names the truncated/excluded docs so a deal team reading "no conflicts" knows whether the scan saw the whole CIM. The cross-ref auto-run on each analysis completion (already shipped in [/api/analyze/stream](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) for both deals + packages) keeps its 30-minute cooldown; per-user rate-limit raised to 20/hr (from 5/hr) on both POST endpoints.
- **Founder Hub permanent chat pane (2026-04-23):** [FounderChatWidget](src/components/founder-hub/FounderChatWidget.tsx) accepts a `variant: 'floating' | 'pane'` prop. At ≥1280px on `/dashboard/founder-hub`, the chat renders as a permanent right-rail panel (340px sticky column) instead of the floating bubble. State persisted via `localStorage['di-founder-hub-chat-pane']`. Below 1280px, falls back to the floating MessageSquare bubble. Conversation history + starters unchanged.
- **Thinking Partners — multi-persona reasoning lens (locked 2026-05-03):** the FounderChatWidget gained a switchable persona picker in the header. Same `FOUNDER_CONTEXT` grounding stays loaded on every request; what changes is the LENS the AI reasons through. Four personas in [src/lib/data/thinking-partners.ts](src/lib/data/thinking-partners.ts): `default` (legacy decision coach — preserves prior behaviour for first-load + unknown-id fallback), `cognitive_psychologist` (Kahneman / Klein / Tetlock / Lovallo / Mercier & Sperber — paper-citation-dense; pressure-tests R²F operationalisations from the inside), `business_strategist` (Porter / Christensen / Helmer / Roger Martin / Mauborgne & Kim / Dunford — MECE structure; tests the strategic logic behind every move), `skeptical_investor` (Sequoia / a16z / Founders Fund / Bessemer-grade Series A diligence — blunt; demands evidence not narrative; ends every probe with PASS/WATCH/TAKE-TO-PARTNERS verdict). **Wiring**: [POST /api/founder-hub/chat](src/app/api/founder-hub/chat/route.ts) accepts optional `personaId` in JSON body OR FormData (multipart upload path); unknown / missing ids fall back to `default` so old clients keep working unchanged. The persona's `systemPrompt` REPLACES the legacy hardcoded coach instruction; FOUNDER_CONTEXT + recent-meetings block stay loaded above. **UI**: header badge becomes a clickable picker → opens an in-flow panel below the header listing all 4 personas with icon + label + discipline + 1-line whatItIsFor + 3 anchor chips. Active persona's color flows through the bubble accent + send-button + user-message bubble + floating-chat-button shadow so the lens choice is visible at a glance from across the screen. Persona persists in `localStorage['founder-chat-persona']` independently from messages, so switching mid-conversation keeps the thread — the same memo gets challenged by Kahneman, then Porter, then a Sequoia partner. Per-persona starter prompts on the empty-state. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a 5th persona, append to `THINKING_PARTNERS` with stable id (no renumbering — the union type catches consumers) + at least 4 named source anchors + a distinct voice rule + 3 specific challenge moves + 4-6 starter prompts. Generic "act as a PhD" prompts produce generic output; the moat lives in the source-anchoring. Voice realtime back-and-forth (WebRTC + low-latency TTS+STT + interruption handling) is the next ship on this surface — explicit founder ask 2026-05-03, scoped pre-seed-critical despite the prior "defer past pre-seed" lock.
- **Voice mode — LiveKit + Cartesia + Deepgram + Grok via separate Railway worker (locked 2026-05-03):** the FounderChatWidget gained a mic toggle in the input row that opens an in-flow voice session within the same chat shell (replaces the input row, conversation history persists above). **Architecture**: browser → WebRTC → LiveKit Cloud → Railway-hosted worker → Deepgram Nova-3 STT + Grok 4.3 via Vercel AI Gateway (OpenAI-compatible) + Cartesia Sonic-2 TTS → back through LiveKit → browser. The worker lives in [voice-worker/](voice-worker/) as a separate Node app NOT bundled with the Vercel main app — Vercel serverless can't host a long-running LiveKit-Agents process. **Per-persona voice profiles** in [thinking-partners.ts](src/lib/data/thinking-partners.ts) `VoiceProfile`: cognitive psychologist → British academic (slower 0.9× speed, 140-word turns to land citations); business strategist → US executive (neutral pace, 120w); skeptical investor → fast NYC partner (1.15× pace, 80w blunt); default coach → warm conversational (100w). Each voice ID is overridable via env var (`CARTESIA_VOICE_PSYCHOLOGIST` etc.) so the founder swaps voices in Railway dashboard without redeploying. **Source-of-truth contract**: the worker is INTENTIONALLY THIN — it calls [GET /api/founder-hub/voice-context?personaId=X](src/app/api/founder-hub/voice-context/route.ts) at session start to pull `FOUNDER_CONTEXT` + persona system prompt + voice-mode addendum + recent meetings. Single source of truth lives in the main app; positioning locks + persona prompt edits propagate to voice mode on the next session start without redeploying the worker. The voice-context endpoint is auth-gated by `VOICE_WORKER_SECRET` shared between Vercel + Railway (Bearer header). **Voice-mode addendum** in [`buildVoiceModeAddendum`](src/lib/data/thinking-partners.ts) augments each persona's text-mode systemPrompt with: per-persona word cap, plain-spoken-prose rule (no markdown / bullets / dashes — TTS reads them literally), citation discipline (speak short form `per Kahneman & Klein 2009`, not full bibliographic ref — full citation appears in transcript), interruption-recovery directive (on barge-in pivot, don't restart the prior sentence), and the persona's voiceRule preserved. **UI**: [VoiceModePanel](src/components/founder-hub/voice/VoiceModePanel.tsx) is lazy-loaded — the ~200KB livekit-client bundle only ships on first mic-toggle activation, not on every chat-widget mount. Live captions stream via LiveKit `TranscriptionReceived` events disambiguated by participant identity (`founder` vs agent). Mute toggle, session timer with 25-min warning + 30-min hard cap (matches JWT TTL + worker-side `setTimeout`), end-session button. On disconnect the accumulated transcript is spliced back into the chat message history so the same thread continues seamlessly between voice and text. **Cost**: ~$80-180/mo at 1.5-2 hr/day (Cartesia is the biggest line; Grok via existing AI Gateway adds ~$30-60/mo with prompt caching on `FOUNDER_CONTEXT`; Deepgram ~$10-15/mo; LiveKit Cloud free tier covers single-user; Railway worker $5/mo). Per-session metrics log to stdout in JSON via [SessionMetrics](voice-worker/src/metrics.ts) — grep `[voice-worker:end]` in Railway logs for per-session cost projections. **Deferred from this lock**: persistent spend dashboard (needs a Prisma model — founder approval before schema change per CLAUDE.md "Modifying schema" rule); monthly kill switch (admin setting). **Forward-looking rules**: (a) when CLAUDE.md positioning vocabulary or persona system prompts change, update [thinking-partners.ts](src/lib/data/thinking-partners.ts) — the worker auto-picks up the edit on the next session start, no redeploy needed. (b) When LiveKit Agents Node SDK upgrades and the import surface shifts, the change is localised to [voice-worker/src/agent.ts](voice-worker/src/agent.ts) imports + `VoicePipelineAgent` constructor — context-loading + system-prompt assembly is stable across versions. (c) When adding a new persona, set its `voiceProfile` (default Cartesia voice ID + envVar + speed + maxWordsPerVoiceTurn) in the same commit as the new persona definition; voice mode picks it up automatically.
- **Inline post-upload reveal:** After an upload completes on `/dashboard`, the hero zone renders [InlineAnalysisResultCard](src/components/analysis/InlineAnalysisResultCard.tsx) in place of the dropzone — DQI via [ScoreReveal](src/components/ui/ScoreReveal.tsx) (1.2s suspense + grade badge), noise score chip, top-3 biases sorted by severity, and a "Deep Dive" link to `/documents/[id]`. The dashboard accumulates detected biases in `detectedBiasesRef` from the `onBiasDetected` SSE callback and stores the snapshot in `lastCompletedAnalysis` state. Dismissing the card returns to the upload zone; starting a new upload resets the refs. **Do not navigate away from the dashboard on analysis-complete** — the inline reveal IS the wow moment; navigation to `/documents/[id]` only happens when the user opts in via Deep Dive or the notification.

- **Document-detail Timeline phase scrub (2026-04-23):** New temporal axis at the top of `/documents/[id]`, above the Executive Summary. Three phases: `before` (default; the full analyst/cso/board surface), `during` (swaps the body for `PhaseDuringPanel` — the human-decision record, or a stub prompting `/dashboard/cognitive-audits/submit`), `after` (swaps for `PhaseAfterPanel` — recalibrated DQI + Brier + lessons, or a stub prompting `/dashboard/outcome-flywheel`). Persists via `?phase=before|during|after` URL param + `localStorage['di-doc-phase']`. **Phase is independent of viewMode** — a user can be in CSO + during mode, Analyst + after mode, etc., but the viewMode-gated content blocks (CSO/Analyst/Board) only render when `phase === 'before'`. Scrub component: [TimelinePhaseScrub](src/components/documents/TimelinePhaseScrub.tsx) with `PhaseDuringPanel` and `PhaseAfterPanel` co-located. `PhaseAfterPanel` reads `recalibratedDqi` + `outcome.outcome` + `outcome.lessonsLearned` off the analysis row when `outcomeStatus === 'outcome_logged'`. `PhaseDuringPanel` currently shows a stub in every case; wiring it to pull the linked HumanDecision via `/api/human-decisions?analysisId=X` is deferred — that API doesn't currently filter by analysisId/documentId (follow-up).

- **Landing-page narrative lock (2026-04-21 late-afternoon refactor — supersedes all prior locks; adds Kahneman × Klein synthesis beat):** the landing page `/` runs a 9-beat narrative arc. **Beats in order:** (01) Hero — tight typography, eyebrow "For strategy teams who answer to the board", H1 + subhead locked, no inline graph; (02) [ProblemScenes](src/components/marketing/ProblemScenes.tsx) on dark-navy — three broad-enterprise pain scenes; (03) [CategoryTurn](src/components/marketing/CategoryTurn.tsx) white interstitial — "Your data has governance. Your reasoning doesn't."; (04) [KahnemanKleinSynthesis](src/components/marketing/KahnemanKleinSynthesis.tsx) — the IP moat beat: the only platform combining Kahneman's debiasing with Klein's Recognition-Primed Decision framework in one pipeline (biasDetective + noiseJudge + statisticalJury on Kahneman's side, rpdRecognition + forgottenQuestions + pre-mortem on Klein's side, arbitrated by metaJudge). Two-column layout: copy left + convergent cluster viz right. This is the slide-2 pitch-deck claim — no competitor (Cloverpop, Palantir, IBM Watson) combines both traditions. Do NOT dilute this beat with feature copy; keep it framework-first; (05) [MomentsPyramid](src/components/marketing/MomentsPyramid.tsx) — Pyramid-style vertical alternating panels, **five moments** each with a bespoke SVG illustration in [src/components/marketing/moments/](src/components/marketing/moments/): (01) DecisionGraphViz (rich layered temporal graph: 3 quarter-rings, mixed decision/bias/outcome node shapes, live +1 Q4 node), (02) BoardroomViz, (03) AuditTraceViz, (04) DqiGaugeViz (counterfactual / what-if), (05) OutcomeLoopViz (Brier calibration + loop-closure); (06) What-we-replace before/after card (inline, unchanged); (07) Security beat — [SecurityLifecycleStrip](src/components/marketing/SecurityLifecycleStrip.tsx) dynamic 4-stage animated flow sitting ABOVE the refactored CredibilityTrio cards; (08) Proof via [CaseStudyCarousel](src/components/marketing/CaseStudyCarousel.tsx); (09) Close — FAQ + CompetitorComparison → final CTA + Newsletter → Footer. **Pricing is NOT on the landing** (cut 2026-04-21 — reads as desperate; live on `/pricing` only; nav + footer + final CTA link there). **Floating overlay:** [ScrollRevealGraph](src/components/marketing/ScrollRevealGraph.tsx) — 320×320 bottom-right panel on desktop ≥1024px. **Rewritten 2026-04-22 (third pass, final) from a live-audit mockup to an "anatomy of a call" capability constellation:** the live-audit version read as a cheap dashboard mockup and sat on top of the competitor-comparison / FAQ beats. Replaced with an ambient, abstract visualization — a central green "DI" core glyph with five rigor-layer tiles (Graph, Boardroom, Audit, What-if, Outcome) arranged in a pentagon around it. As the reader scrolls, each tile lights up and threads an edge inward; ambient pulse particles flow from each active node toward the core; once all five are active the core ring pulses slowly and the caption reads "EVERY ANGLE · ONE CALL". Eyebrow label: `Decision Intel · anatomy of a call`. Subtitle cycles through the active capability's full name. 6 stages: `STAGE_THRESHOLDS = [0, 0.08, 0.18, 0.28, 0.4, 0.55]`: (0) quiet core only; (1) Knowledge Graph activates; (2) Boardroom; (3) Reasoning audit; (4) What-if; (5) Outcome loop — fully composed. **Visibility range narrowed to `0.04 < scrollProgress < 0.72`** so the overlay fades out before the competitor comparison, FAQ, and final CTA block — no more overlap with actionable content. Dismissible, click-to-expand modal still shows the full 3D [HeroDecisionGraph](src/components/marketing/HeroDecisionGraph.tsx) (WeWork S-1 sample). Respects `prefers-reduced-motion`. Mobile/tablet: hidden. **Live-audit / portfolio-preview / abstract-node variants all retired** — the constellation is the final form. **Palette progression:** white → navy (02) → white (03) → slate-50 (04 synthesis) → slate/white alternation (05, 5 panels) → slate-50 (06) → navy (07) → white (08) → slate-50/navy (close). **Cut from landing:** inline 4-chip trust strip, [CategoryGapShowcase](src/components/marketing/CategoryGapShowcase.tsx) usage, inline HeroDecisionGraph embed, inline pricing section + `handleCheckout`. **Still banned:** Stats bar, PipelineLandingTeaser, OutcomeDetectionViz, Features cards, mid-page BookDemoCTA, startup voice, `agent`/`LangGraph`/`12-node`/`3 independent AI judges` language outside `/how-it-works`. Hero H1 + subhead remain canon.
- **`/demo` route — actual location is `src/app/demo/page.tsx` (NOT under the `(marketing)` route group).** This is a 2,800-line client component that already does paste-first flow with [PasteAuditResults](src/components/marketing/demo/PasteAuditResults.tsx), [scanForPii](src/lib/utils/redaction-scanner.ts), [RedactionPreModal](src/components/ui/RedactionPreModal.tsx), the existing sample picker, and the deep-dive `/demo/[slug]` cards. The 2026-04-25 P0 audit claimed `/demo` 404s because the auditor only checked `src/app/(marketing)/demo/` (which only contains `[slug]/`). The flat `src/app/demo/` directory was missed — `/demo` has been live the whole time. **Do NOT create `src/app/(marketing)/demo/page.tsx`** — Next.js treats route groups as transparent for URL resolution, so `/(marketing)/demo` and `/demo` both resolve to the same `/demo` URL and the build fails with "two parallel pages." This trap was hit twice (2026-04-25 morning P0 restore + the same morning's deploy after CI fixes). When working on `/demo` improvements, edit the existing client component at `src/app/demo/page.tsx` directly. The famous-decision deep-view route at `src/app/(marketing)/demo/[slug]/page.tsx` is untouched and stays. **`/api/demo/run` is SSE-streamed (locked 2026-05-17 — core-flow friction audit #1).** It mirrors `/api/analyze/stream`: same `analyzeDocument(documentId, onProgress)` (zero change to the audit or persistence — only the transport), `formatSSE` + `formatSSEHeartbeat`, terminal `type:'complete'` event carrying `{ documentId, analysisId, result }`, `type:'error'` carrying the message. The client (`demo/page.tsx runPasteAudit`) consumes it with the shared `SSEReader` and drives `pasteStageIdx` from the **real** `progress` number. **Never reintroduce a decoupled progress timer** — the prior fake `setInterval` cycler (every 5500ms, capped) could visibly desync from the real pipeline on the highest-leverage acquisition surface (a stranger pasting a memo); the SSE stream is the single source of truth. Pre-stream guards (env 503 / IP+global rate-limit 429 / word 400/413) still return JSON before the stream opens — the client checks `!res.ok` first, then reads the stream.

- **Marketing copy discipline — no named-prospect leaks (locked 2026-04-25, hardened 2026-04-26):** This is the single most important discipline rule on marketing surfaces. **Never** ship a public route, page title, JSON-LD entry, metadata description, visible HTML copy, OR any source-code comment in a shipped client bundle that names a specific prospect or design-partner ("Sankore", "Wiz", any other firm we have not closed publicly), or any "{firm}-class buyers" coding pattern. Three real catches in the 2026-04-25 + 2026-04-26 audits: `security/page.tsx:464` rendered "Sankore-class buyers" in the hero subhead; `WelcomeModal.tsx:28-31` carried a "Sankore is the design partner" comment that ships in the production bundle; and the persona-audit's recommended "promote the Sankore brief to a public `/sankore` page" was queued before the founder caught it. The right delivery shape for a prospect-specific brief is a private channel (PDF email, token-gated link with `noindex`, in-call screen-share) or a generic page that doesn't name the prospect (e.g. `/for-funds`). Comments must be role-neutral — say "the fund/investor persona identified in design-partner research", not the prospect name. The brief in [src/components/founder-hub/sankore/](src/components/founder-hub/sankore/) stays inside the founder hub. When a future audit recommends building a public page named after any prospect, evaluate against this rule first — the persona is recommending a need, not a delivery shape.
- **DPR architecture lock — McKinsey-grade rebuild (locked 2026-05-05, ALL FOUR PHASES SHIPPED):** the production DPR is being rebuilt as a McKinsey-grade procurement deliverable. Prior generator at [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) (1,696 LOC jsPDF) is dev-grade typography; the legacy sample script at [scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs](scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs) (1,069 LOC) is the same. Both will be retired in Phase 4. **Architecture decisions (locked):** (1) **Rendering tech: HTML/CSS via Next.js route** at [/dpr-render/[type]/[id]](src/app/dpr-render/[type]/[id]/page.tsx) + Tailwind 4 + Inter (body) + Source Serif 4 (display) + JetBrains Mono (hashes), all loaded via @fontsource (local, GDPR-safe). Server PDF generation via puppeteer-core + @sparticuz/chromium-min at [/api/dpr/render-pdf](src/app/api/dpr/render-pdf/route.ts) (Vercel-compatible, ~50MB chromium binary downloaded at first invocation). Client-side export via window.print() after opening the route in a new tab. Build-time sample PDFs via full puppeteer in a script (Phase 4). NOT react-pdf (typography ceiling lower, slow iteration loop, no Tailwind reuse). NOT jsPDF (current; insufficient quality). **Why HTML/CSS wins**: the browser is the most powerful typography engine ever built; CSS hot-reload makes iteration 10× faster than re-rendering PDFs; reuses existing Tailwind / shadcn / Lucide / Inter from the project. Cold start cost ~1-3s on Vercel; warm ~300ms. Memory rule saved: `feedback-best-not-simplest` — choose the best option for the use case, not the simplest infrastructure. (2) **Page architecture: LEGAL-EVIDENCE-RECORD STYLE, not McKinsey-deck.** Per master KB synthesis (NotebookLM 2026-05-05): "Executive buyers and procurement gatekeepers do not want to see the AI's opinion first; they want to see the cryptographic and methodological provenance that proves the document's legal defensibility." Page order locked: (page 1) cover + cryptographic integrity (record-id, hashes, schema version, audit timestamp, verification block) — Phase 1 SHIPPED; (page 2) methodological defensibility (judge variance / noise stats / model lineage / prompt fingerprint) — Phase 2; (page 3) R²F procurement strips (Validity / Reference Class / Feedback Adequacy / Org Calibration / Counterfactual Impact) — Phase 2; (pages 4-N) per-bias finding cards with severity meter (5-segment) + verbatim evidence quote + **"Harden with:" audit-committee-ready hardening question** + regulatory mapping + mitigation — Phase 3; (page N+1) Structural Assumptions Dalio cards — Phase 3; (page N+2) Regulatory Crosswalk grid (19-framework registry across G7/EU/GCC/African markets) — Phase 3; (page N+3) Reviewer Decisions HITL log — Phase 4 retro-fit; (page N+4) Package/deal members — Phase 4; (page N+5) Data Lifecycle footer — Phase 4. (3) **Color palette: severity-led, Kahneman-grade contrast.** Per Kahneman: "If you use color, you are more likely to be believed if your text is printed in bright blue or red than in middling shades of green, yellow, or pale blue." Bright red (#dc2626) for critical, bright blue (#2563eb) for high (Kahneman optimum), amber (#d97706) for medium, restrained green for low/positive only. Navy 900 (#0a0e27) brand band stays as anchor; warm grey 100-950 for hierarchy. DI green DEMOTED from decoration to severity-low only. (4) **Typography pairing**: Inter Variable body + Source Serif 4 Variable display (free, @fontsource) + JetBrains Mono Variable for hashes. High-contrast Kahneman-grade legibility on every text run. Tokens locked in [src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css](src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css). (5) **Per-finding card structure (locked)**: severity meter (5-segment horizontal bar) + verbatim evidence quote + "Harden with:" hardening question (template library indexed by bias type, NOT LLM-generated per-call) + regulatory mapping + mitigation suggestion. (6) **Vocabulary discipline (cross-confirmed)**: "tamper-evident today, private-key signing on Q3 2026 roadmap" — never "signed"; "aligned with AI Verify" — never "certified"; "SOC 2 Type II infrastructure" — never "SOC 2 certified"; replace cold "Brier 0.258" with "143-case reference-class corpus from primary sources". META-RULE: "honest disclosures are a procurement weapon — overclaims destroy trust." **Shipped state (Phase 4 ship 2026-05-05):** **15 physical pages** of McKinsey-grade typography rendering on `/dpr-render/[type]/[id]`. Phase 1 = page 1 cover + cryptographic integrity. Phase 2 = page 2 methodological defensibility (judge variance + model lineage) + page 3 R²F procurement strips (5 strips: Validity / Reference Class / Feedback Adequacy / Org Calibration / Counterfactual Impact). Phase 3 = page 4 per-bias finding cards (severity meter + verbatim evidence + Harden-with hardening question + regulatory mapping + mitigation) + page 5 Dalio Structural Assumptions + page 6 19-framework Regulatory Crosswalk grid by region. Phase 4 = wire-in across all consumers + retired legacy + Dangote specimen. **Active surfaces (all 6 consumers wired)**: `/api/public/sample-dpr` (Phase 2 swap, public specimen, rate-limited 10/hr/IP) · `/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4, Pro-plan-gated, audit-logged, external-share notification preserved) · `/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4) · `/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4) · `/api/compliance/audit-packet/[analysisId]` (Phase 4, legacy URL kept stable) · `/documents/[id]` Export DPR button (Phase 4, blob-URL download). All 6 consumers go through the shared `renderDprPdf()` helper at [src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts](src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts), forwarding the caller's Supabase auth cookie to the headless Chromium so `/dpr-render/document|package|deal/[id]` re-verifies ownership server-side as defense-in-depth. **Specimens**: `/dpr-render/specimen/wework` (canonical S-1 retro, Project Heliograph DACH narrative) + `/dpr-render/specimen/dangote` (Pan-African industrial expansion narrative, locked 2026-05-05 P4 #4). Both regenerate `public/dpr-sample-{wework,dangote}.pdf` via `node scripts/dev-dpr-preview.mjs` against the running dev server. **Data flow**: `assembleProvenanceRecordData` (+ Package + Deal variants) now populates `findingsAugment: Record<biasType, { evidenceQuote, mitigation, severityOverride, confidenceOverride }>` from `analysis.biases` (excerpt + suggestion + severity + confidence). The /dpr-render route reads `data.findingsAugment` for real audits, falls back to `SAMPLE_FINDINGS_AUGMENT` / `DANGOTE_FINDINGS_AUGMENT` for specimens. Single deriver path: `deriveDprFindings(data, augment)` joins citations + regulatoryMapping + counterfactualImpact + the hardening-question template library at [src/lib/reports/dpr-hardening-questions.ts](src/lib/reports/dpr-hardening-questions.ts) (15 canonical bias→hardening-question mappings, indexed by bias type, NOT LLM-generated per audit). **Client-Safe Export Mode**: `?clientSafe=1` query param flows from API consumer → `/dpr-render` route → classification chip flips to "Client-safe export" + redaction logic engages (entity / amount / person-name placeholders for the meta strip + summary; redaction within finding cards is a follow-up since the per-bias evidence quotes already get authored under the no-named-prospects discipline). **Legacy retirement**: the 1,696-LOC `decision-provenance-record-generator.ts` (jsPDF) is no longer called by any active code path — only doc / comment references remain. The 1,069-LOC `scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs` no longer generates DPR samples (only DPA template + DOCX); the buildDprSample + buildDprDangote functions are retained as emergency fallback but commented out of the run path. **Forward-looking rule**: when any visual / typography / color / layout decision changes, update [src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css](src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css) only — every page component reads from these CSS-variable tokens. When a new consumer surface needs a DPR PDF, import `renderDprPdf` from [src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts](src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts) — never re-import the legacy jsPDF generator.

- **Trust-copy single source of truth (locked 2026-04-26, extended 2026-05-01):** [src/lib/constants/trust-copy.ts](src/lib/constants/trust-copy.ts) is the canonical home for procurement-stage security claims that appear on multiple marketing surfaces. - **DPR vocabulary lock — "hashed + tamper-evident", NOT "signed + hashed" (locked 2026-04-26):** the 2026-04-26 persona audit (James + Margaret) caught "signed, hashed" overclaim across 16 surfaces. The implementation in [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) produces SHA-256 input hashes; it does NOT cryptographically sign with a Decision Intel private key. Until private-key signing ships, every consumer must describe the artefact as "hashed + tamper-evident" — see `DPR_PROVENANCE_*` constants. When private-key signing ships, restore "signed" by updating the constants in `trust-copy.ts` and the explanatory header in `provenance-record-data.ts`.

Wired into [MarketingNav](src/components/marketing/MarketingNav.tsx) (Enterprise mega-menu), the landing-page footer, and [sitemap.ts](src/app/sitemap.ts).
- **Privacy-policy GDPR Art 13 mandatory disclosures (added 2026-04-26):** [/privacy](<src/app/(marketing)/privacy/page.tsx>) carries the four disclosures GDPR Art 13 requires: (1) Controller identity block — pulls from `company-info.ts`; (2) Lawful Basis section — `LAWFUL_BASIS` array maps each processing activity to its Art 6 basis; (3) Right to lodge a supervisory complaint (Art 77) — bottom of the Rights section, links to ICO / CNIL / Irish DPC / Nigerian NITDA / SA Information Regulator; (4) International Transfers section — names DPF, SCCs, IDTA, NDPR-transfer agreements, PoPIA s.72. The processors list also gained `Resend` and `Cloudflare` (sub-processors James caught as missing under Art 28(3)(d)). When adding a new processing activity (new product feature, new analytics path, new sub-processor), update LAWFUL_BASIS + PROCESSORS in the same commit so the privacy page never drifts from the actual data flows. Also: GDPR rights array gained an Art 22 automated-decision-contestation card.
- **Cross-reference auto-trigger 30-min cooldown (parity, 2026-04-26):** [/api/analyze/stream](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) auto-fires a deal cross-reference when an analysis completes on a deal with ≥2 analyzed docs. The 2026-04-26 audit caught the deal-side missing the package-side's 30-min cooldown — meaning back-to-back uploads could fire N runs at ~£0.40 Gemini cost each. Both deal + package now check `dealCrossReference.findFirst({ runAt: { gt: now - 30min } })` before firing. The manual button on the deal page bypasses the cooldown via its own per-user 20/hr rate limit. **Note**: Marcus's 2026-04-26 audit incorrectly claimed cross-reference was manual-only — the auto-trigger has shipped since 3.1 deep. CLAUDE.md was right; the audit was wrong (verification miss on the analyze/stream route). Always grep the route before claiming a feature is missing.
- **EU/Multi-region quote builder honesty (locked 2026-04-26):** the public + admin EnterpriseQuoteBuilder UI still offers `US`, `EU`, and `Multi-region`. Production today runs Vercel + Supabase US. When the user picks EU or Multi-region, an inline amber-tinted disclaimer surfaces in the form and the rendered PDF (a) labels the Region row as "EU (Enterprise-conversation residency, not production today)" and (b) appends a short italic note in the contracted-artefacts section explaining what the picked preference actually means. The server-side coercion to `US` was REMOVED — the user's pick is honoured in the PDF, with the disclaimer making it impossible for a procurement reader to interpret it as a current-state guarantee. Until EU residency is actually provisioned, leave both layers (UI inline disclaimer + PDF clarifying note) intact.
- **Document-detail mobile (locked 2026-04-26):** the [/documents/[id]](<src/app/(platform)/documents/[id]/page.tsx>) main grid (`gridTemplateColumns: '1fr 380px'`) and the tab bar (`flex-wrap + overflow:hidden`) BOTH had no mobile breakpoint. On phones the sidebar column crushed the main content and the tab bar silently clipped the second row of tabs. Fix shipped 2026-04-26: classes `doc-detail-main-grid` + `doc-detail-tab-bar` plus a scoped `<style>` block at the bottom of the page with a `@media (max-width: 900px)` rule that stacks the grid to a single column and switches the tab bar to horizontal scroll. **Don't add new top-level inline styles** that override these classes on the same elements without also adding a matching mobile override; the `<style>` block is the single mobile override and has to win on the narrow viewport.
